If the cookiejar has recorded the next timestamp at which one or\\n379:  * more cookies expire, then processing will exit early in case this timestamp\\n380:  * is in the future.\\n381:  */\\n382: static void remove_expired(struct CookieInfo *cookies)\\n383: {\\n384:   struct Cookie *co, *nx;\\n385:   curl_off_t now = (curl_off_t)time(NULL);\\n386:   unsigned int i;\\n387: \\n388:   /*\\n389:    * If the earliest expiration timestamp in the jar is in the future we can\\n390:    * skip scanning the whole jar and instead exit early as there won't be any\\n391:    * cookies to evict.  If we need to evict however, reset the next_expiration\\n392:    * counter in order to track the next one. In case the recorded first\\n393:    * expiration is the max offset, then perform the safe fallback of checking\\n394:    * all cookies.\\n395:    */\\n396:   if(now < cookies->next_expiration &&\\n397:       cookies->next_expiration != CURL_OFF_T_MAX)\\n398:     return;\\n399:   else\\n400:     cookies->next_expiration = CURL_OFF_T_MAX;\\n401: \\n402:   for(i = 0; The caller is responsible for checking\\n361:  * for OOM errors.\\n362:  */\\n363: static void strstore(char **str, const char *newstr, size_t len)\\n364: {\\n365:   DEBUGASSERT(newstr);\\n366:   DEBUGASSERT(str);\\n367:   free(*str);\\n368:   *str = Curl_memdup(newstr, len + 1);\\n369:   if(*str)\\n370:     (*str)[len] = 0;\\n371: }\\n372: \\n373: /*\\n374:  * remove_expired\\n375:  *\\n376:  * Remove expired cookies from the hash by inspecting the expires timestamp on\\n377:  * each cookie in the hash, freeing and deleting any where the timestamp is in\\n378:  * the past.  If the cookiejar has recorded the next timestamp at which one or\\n379:  * more cookies expire, then processing will exit early in case this timestamp\\n380:  * is in the future.\\n381:  */\\n382: static void remove_expired(struct CookieInfo *cookies)\\n383: {\\n384:   struct Cookie *co, *nx;\\n385:   curl_off_t now = (curl_off_t)time(NULL);\\n386:   unsigned int i;\\n387: \\n388:   /*\\n389:    * If the earliest expiration timestamp in the jar is in the future we can\\n390:    * skip scanning the whole jar and instead exit early as there won't be any\\n391:    * cookies to evict.  If we need to evict however, reset the next_expiration\\n392:    * counter in order to track the next one. In case the recorded first\\n393:    * expiration is the max offset, then perform the safe fallback of checking\\n394:    * all cookies.\\n395:    */\\n396:   if(now < cookies->next_expiration &&\\n397:       cookies->next_expiration != CURL_OFF_T_MAX)\\n398:     return;\\n399:   else\\n400:     cookies->next_expiration = CURL_OFF_T_MAX;\\n401: \\n402:   for(i = 0; i < COOKIE_HASH_SIZE; i++) {\\n403:     struct Cookie *pv = NULL;\\n404:     co = cookies->cookies[i];\\n405:     while(co) {\\n406:       nx = co->next;\\n407:       if(co->expires && co->expires < now) {\\n408:         if(!pv) {\\n409:           cookies->cookies[i] = co->next;\\n410:         }\\n411:         else {\\n412:           pv->next = co->next;\\n413:         }\\n414:         cookies->numcookies--;\\n415:         freecookie(co);\\n416:       }\\n417:       else {\\n418:         /*\\n419:          * If this cookie has an expiration timestamp earlier than what we've\\n420:          * seen so far then record it for the next round of expirations.\\n421:          */\\n422:         if(co->expires && co->expires < cookies->next_expiration)\\n423:           cookies->next_expiration = co->expires;\\n424:         pv = co;\\n425:       }\\n426:       co = nx;\\n427:     }\\n428:   }\\n429: }\\n430: \\n431: /* Make sure domain contains a dot or is localhost. */\\n432: static bool bad_domain(const char *domain, size_t len)\\n433: {\\n434:   if((len == 9) && strncasecompare(domain, \\\"localhost\\\", 9))\\n435:     return FALSE;\\n436:   else {\\n437:     /* there must be a dot present, but that dot must not be a trailing dot */\\n438:     char *dot = memchr(domain, '.', len);\\n439:     if(dot) {\\n440:       size_t i = dot - domain;\\n441:       if((len - i) > 1)\\n442:         /* the dot is not the last byte */\\n443:         return FALSE;\\n444:     }\\n445:   }\\n446:   return TRUE;\\n447: }\\n448: \\n449: /*\\n450:   RFC 6265 section 4.1.1 says a server should accept this range:\\n451: \\n452:   cookie-octet    = %x21 / %x23-2B / %x2D-3A / %x3C-5B / %x5D-7E\\n453: \\n454:   But Firefox and Chrome as of June 2022 accept space, comma and double-quotes\\n455:   fine. The Domain Attribute says:\n140:    * For example, if the value of the Domain attribute is\n141:    * \"example.com\", the user agent will include the cookie in the Cookie\n142:    * header when making HTTP requests to example.com, www.example.com, and\n143:    * www.corp.example.com.\n144:    */\n145:   if(hostname_len == cookie_domain_len)\n146:     return TRUE;\n147:   if('.' == *(hostname + hostname_len - cookie_domain_len - 1))\n148:     return TRUE;\n149:   return FALSE;\n150: }\n151: \n152: /*\n153:  * matching cookie path and url path\n154:  * RFC6265 5.1.4 Paths and Path-Match\n155:  */\n156: static bool pathmatch(const char *cookie_path, const char *request_uri)\n157: {\n158:   size_t cookie_path_len;\n159:   size_t uri_path_len;\n160:   char *uri_path = NULL;\n161:   char *pos;\n162:   bool ret = FALSE;\n163: \n164:   /* cookie_path must not have last '/' separator. ex: /sample */\n165:   cookie_path_len = strlen(cookie_path);\n166:   if(1 == cookie_path_len) {\n167:     /* cookie_path must be '/' */\n168:     return TRUE;\n169:   }\n170: \n171:   uri_path = strdup(request_uri);\n172:   if(!uri_path)\n173:     return FALSE;\n174:   pos = strchr(uri_path, '?');\n175:   if(pos)\n176:     *pos = 0x0;\n177: \n178:   /* #-fragments are already cut off! */\n179:   if(0 == strlen(uri_path) || uri_path[0] != '/') {\n180:     strstore(&uri_path, \"/\", 1);\n181:     if(!uri_path)\n182:       return FALSE;\n183:   }\n184: \n185:   /*\n186:    * here, RFC6265 5.1.4 says\n187:    *  4. If the cookiejar has recorded the next timestamp at which one or\n379:  * more cookies expire, then processing will exit early in case this timestamp\n380:  * is in the future.\n381:  */\n382: static void remove_expired(struct CookieInfo *cookies)\n383: {\n384:   struct Cookie *co, *nx;\n385:   curl_off_t now = (curl_off_t)time(NULL);\n386:   unsigned int i;\n387: \n388:   /*\n389:    * If the earliest expiration timestamp in the jar is in the future we can\n390:    * skip scanning the whole jar and instead exit early as there won't be any\n391:    * cookies to evict. Meanwhile, we have to call Curl_read\n447:        to ensure that http2_handle_stream_close is called when we read all\n448:        incoming bytes for a particular stream. */\n449:     bool is_http3 = Curl_conn_is_http3(data, conn, FIRSTSOCKET);\n450:     data_eof_handled = is_http3 || Curl_conn_is_http2(data, conn, FIRSTSOCKET);\n451: \n452:     if(!data_eof_handled && k->size != -1 && !k->header) {\n453:       /* make sure we don't read too much */\n454:       curl_off_t totalleft = k->size - k->bytecount;\n455:       if(totalleft < (curl_off_t)bytestoread)\n456:         bytestoread = (size_t)totalleft;\n457:     }\n458: \n459:     if(bytestoread) {\n460:       /* receive data from the network! */\n461:       result = Curl_read(data, conn->sockfd, buf, bytestoread, &nread);\n462: \n463:       /* read would've blocked */\n464:       if(CURLE_AGAIN == result) {\n465:         result = CURLE_OK;\n466:         break; /* get out of loop */\n467:       }\n468: \n469:       if(result>0)\n470:         goto out;\n471:     }\n472:     else {\n473:       /* read nothing but since we wanted nothing we consider this an OK\n474:          situation to proceed from */\n475:       DEBUGF(infof(data, \"readwrite_data: we're done\"));\n476:       nread = 0;\n477:     }\n478: \n479:     if(!k->bytecount) {\n480:       Curl_pgrsTime(data, TIMER_STARTTRANSFER);\n481:       if(k->exp100 > EXP100_SEND_DATA)\n482:         /* set time stamp to compare with when waiting for the 100 */\n483:         k->start100 = Curl_now();\n484:     }\n485: \n486:     *didwhat |= KEEP_RECV;\n487:     /* indicates data of zero size, i.e. empty file */\n488:     is_empty_data = ((nread == 0) && (k->bodywrites == 0)) ? According to OpenSSL documentation, ASN1_STRING data is not guaranteed to be NULL-terminated.\n\nHowever, line 2224 calls `strlen(altptr)` which assumes NULL termination. If `altptr` is not NULL-terminated, `strlen()` will read past the end of the data until it finds a NULL byte, potentially causing a buffer over-read.\n\nThis is a **buffer over-read vulnerability**!\n\nFix: Don't call strlen on data that may not be NULL-terminated. The code should only use `altlen` which has already been obtained from `ASN1_STRING_length()`.\n\nActually, looking more carefully at the comment (lines 2215-2221), it says:\n```\nIt has been however verified that in 0.9.6 and 0.9.7, IA5String\nis always null-terminated.\n```\n\nBut we can't assume that for all OpenSSL versions.
